The Murderer of Zhao Arrives in Shanghai

Captured in Xiadian Village, Hefei County, Anhui 114

Brought Back by Shen Jinghua, the County Public Security Bureau Chief

Zhao Tieqiao, former commissioner of the China Merchants Bureau, was assassinated in June of this year. The murderer had been at large and had not been apprehended. Recently, Shen Jinghua, the chief of the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau, received a tip-off detailing that the murderer fled to his ancestral home in Xiadian Village, Hefei County, Anhui, after assassinating Zhao. He then dispatched detectives to investigate and confirm the information before personally going to Anhui to make the arrest. Yesterday, Chief Shen and detectives Gu Xingzhou, Chen Yibing, Lü Hailong, and Hou Guicong escorted the captured murderer, Xia Shaoen, back to Shanghai. The details are recorded below:

Brief Biography of the Murderer: The murderer, Xia Shaoen, is 30 years old, from Xiadian Village, 30 li east of Hefei County, Anhui Province. He was a farmer. His father died early, and he has a grandmother over 80 years old, a mother over 60 years old, and a wife, Qian, who is 29 years old. In the spring of the 17th year of the Republic (1928), she came to Shanghai with Xia and gave birth to a daughter, who is now five years old and is being cared for by Xia's mother at home. According to Xia, after arriving in Shanghai in the spring of the 17th year of the Republic, he lived at a certain address on a certain road (the exact address will not be announced for the time being) and made a small business selling face cream. After the incident, he stayed in Shanghai for more than a month to listen to the news. Later, due to the news of the reward for his arrest, the news became more urgent, so he left Shanghai alone and returned to his ancestral home in Anhui. His wife still resides in Shanghai to listen to the news from Shanghai and communicate from time to time.

Details of the Capture: Shen Jinghua, the chief of the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau, believed that although the Zhao case occurred in the concession, he, as a member of the Public Security Bureau, should arrest the true culprit and bring him to justice to fulfill the duties of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau and to prevent the false accusation of others. Therefore, he sent detectives to investigate and learned that Xia Shaoen was the real culprit in the Zhao case and had fled to Hefei. Therefore, on October 18, the county government issued an order to the Public Security Bureau to prepare passports and ordered county detectives Gu Xingzhou, Chen Yibing, and Lü Hailong to take the case passports and a pistol to Hefei to investigate and arrest the suspect. However, after the three men arrived in Hefei, their pistols were exposed in a small teahouse, and the third branch of the Hefei County Public Security Bureau and the Chamber of Commerce Security Corps suspected them of being villains and arrested them. After each of them produced their passports to prove their identity, the Hefei Public Security Bureau telegraphed the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau for confirmation, and the three detectives were released and Xia was arrested. However, due to the remote road of thousands of miles and the difficulty of extraditing prisoners from another province, Chief Shen personally went to Hefei on October 30 with detective Hou Guicong to bring Xia back.

The Situation Along the Way: After Chief Shen arrived in Hefei, he contacted all parties and began escorting the suspect Xia Shaoen by long-distance bus to Wuhu on the night of the 4th of this month with the four detectives who had gone there earlier. On the afternoon of the 7th, they took the Jiang'an steamship of the China Merchants Bureau downstream to Zhenjiang. At 3:30 a.m. on the 8th, Chief Shen transferred to the Beijing-Shanghai train in Zhenjiang and arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning. He went directly to the China Merchants Wharf on the Bund to explain the reason for bringing the prisoner to the police on duty to prevent any unexpected incidents. At 7:10 a.m., the Jiang'an steamship arrived at the shore. Four detectives, Gu Xingzhou, Chen Bingyi, Lü Hailong, and Hou Guicong, escorted Xia to the shore. Chief Shen led the way to the county government and detained him in the Public Security Bureau. Although the murderer has been arrested, the travel expenses and other expenses of Chief Shen and the detectives amount to more than 800 yuan. The fact that Gu, Chen, and Lü were previously detained and tortured by the Third Branch of the Hefei Public Security Bureau still needs to be negotiated after the case is closed.

Appearance of the Murderer: After the murderer Xia Shaoen entered the county Public Security Bureau, Chief Shen ordered him to be detained in the patrol room in the west room downstairs and rented a cotton quilt and blanket for him to keep warm. The reporter of the Daily News wanted to see the appearance of Xia, so he led the secretary and patrol leader of the Public Security Bureau to visit Xia. Xia's face was plump and did not look like a small business owner. His hair was flat-topped, but the hair was long and seemed to be uncut. He wore a blue cloth wrapped around his head, imitating the appearance of a farmer in Anhui Province. He wore a dark blue cotton jacket and pants, which were old and dirty. His eyes showed fierceness and his face was red, indicating that he was uneasy.

Taigu Sailors' Salary Increase

Has Received a Satisfactory Reply 115

Treaty to be Signed Soon

Wang Yongsheng, the guiding committee member of the Shanghai Sailors' Association, visited Yu Qiaqing of the Sanbei Company the day before yesterday to inquire about the results of the Taigu sailors' salary increase. Yu said that he had earnestly negotiated with the Taigu Company and the results are as follows: (1) Taigu agreed to increase the salary by four yuan from September 1st of this year. (2) The draft contract (this is never to increase the salary again) (the Seamen's Union must process the salary increase in March next year) Both parties withdraw this clause. (3) Subsequent requests for assistance from the Seamen's Union must be approved by the union. It is reported that the treaty is scheduled to be formally signed next week.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Telegraphed for Methods to Relieve the Fishing Industry 121

Page 10

Negotiating Japanese Vessels' Encroachment on Fishing

Safeguarding Fishermen's Livelihoods 122

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, Nanjing. A letter from member Jin Chuxiang states: "Millions of people in the coastal provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong rely entirely on fishing for a living. In recent years, piracy has been rampant, customs duties are not good, and anti-smuggling is extorting. Fishermen are suffering from oppression, and millions have lost their jobs. The strong take risks and join bandits, while the weak sit and wait for death, all becoming starving corpses. Although the government is thinking of providing relief, there are no proper methods. Strong powers such as Japan and the United States are taking the opportunity to transport large quantities of fish to China, such as Japanese and Russian salmon and American blue mackerel, etc., amounting to tens of millions of dan per year. Residents find them easy to sell due to their low prices. Domestic fish are subject to heavy taxes and bandit disturbances, so the fishing industry has no possibility of development. This is the indirect killing of our fishermen by imperialists. There are also those who directly kill our fishermen, that is, Japanese fishing vessels that catch fish in the seas of Jiangsu and Zhejiang and transport them to Shanghai for sale at very low prices. There are dozens of such fishing vessels, and they transport very quickly. Merchants are benefiting from the commission, but they do not know that the price of sailboat fish cannot be sold, and the livelihoods of fishermen are exhausted. Six methods are proposed below: (1) Please have the Ministry of Foreign Affairs negotiate with Japan to prevent Japanese vessels from fishing across the sea. (2) Please order the National Government to prohibit fish merchants across the country from selling Japanese vessel fish. (3) Improve salt tax (4) Severely punish smuggling extortion (5) Jointly suppress pirates by land, sea, and air forces (6) Dispatch officials to help fishermen's livelihood and emphasize national rights," etc. The original letter states that the encroachment of Japanese vessels on fishing was initially limited to Zhili and later extended to Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong. When our country negotiated with them, they claimed that the area covered by the fishing vessels was within the scope of the high seas and did not encroach on China's territorial waters. Therefore, after several years, there has been no result, and the interests of our country's fishing industry are being lost day by day. According to the old international law, the width of territorial waters was three nautical miles. Later, with the advancement of firearms, various countries had different opinions on the three-nautical-mile rule and could not strictly abide by it. The Hague Peace Conference convened to compile the League of Nations Law Conference, and there were many disputes about the width of territorial waters, which have not been resolved. The Navy Department believes that the three-nautical-mile rule is sufficient to gain an advantage based on our country's topography, but it has not fully considered the interests of our country's territorial waters and fishing industry or the recent encroachment by the Japanese. It should be requested that the Navy Department be consulted again for a long-term discussion. As for whether the area encroached on by the Japanese over the years is within the scope of the high seas or involves our country's territorial waters, why should we take the word of the Japanese? It should be requested that the Navy Department be consulted to send warships to patrol regularly during the fishing season. If there are Japanese vessels crossing the border, they should be expelled to prevent the sprout of spying. As for the rampant piracy, it is reported in the newspapers every day, and the government should be aware of it without the need for further description. Officials raising soldiers has become a problem of the heart and stomach, and the people along the coast are suffering every day. It should be requested that the Ministry present the case to the court and transfer it to the government to dispatch land, sea, and air forces to conduct a thorough search and suppression to ensure that the roots are completely eradicated and expelled from the country. In this way, the sea frontier will be pacified, and the fishing industry will be blessed. Also, regarding the improvement of the salt tax, according to common practice, the tax rate for industrial salt should be lighter than that for edible salt. Our country has not been able to handle this type of salt separately. Recently, the soy sauce industry has been feeling the burden of the salt tax, and business is increasingly declining. It should be requested that the Ministry of Finance be consulted to re-examine and determine the tax rates for various industrial salts and reduce the collection separately. As for the difficulties in smuggling mentioned in the original letter, the fishing salt used by fishing boats is taxed and issued by the fishing factory, and the ships are distributed according to the certificate. The fish factory transports the certificate back to the official salt ship for cancellation. Therefore, each fishing boat has no certificate to carry, and there have always been precedents for official agencies to check it. In recent years, the Anti-Smuggling Bureau has repeatedly detained fishing boats. Even if the fishing boats are released after citing precedents, the losses of the fishing boats are still considerable. It should be requested that the Ministry of Finance order the anti-smuggling officials to strictly warn that all these situations were not mentioned in the original letter. Adding more explanations is reasonable, and it is appropriate to telegraph and request the Ministry to examine and approve them separately for implementation to maintain the fishing industry for public benefit. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Silk Factory Representatives Return to Shanghai

Meeting to Report Progress Tomorrow 123

The silk factory owners in this port are unable to maintain their business due to the sluggish sales and losses of silk factories and have announced shutdowns by public agreement. It was resolved to request the government to issue 10 million yuan of public bonds for the silk industry in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai to relieve the silk market. Five representatives, including Shen Huachen, Wang Xiaolai, Huang Jinchen, Zhu Jing'an, and Huang Jinfan, were elected to go to Beijing with representatives from Wuxi and other places in Zhejiang to petition. Various Trade Unions

Safeguard the Lives of Workers 124

Order Factories and Shops

Improve Fire Prevention

The various trade unions of Shanghai submitted a document to the Municipal Social Bureau, requesting to seriously

crack down on all factories and shops in the city that do not have adequate fire prevention equipment, and to order each employer to be responsible for protecting the safety of the employees before the equipment is improved, in order to maintain life and prevent danger. The unions have seen the tragic deaths of many workers in the Huakang Road Fuchang Military Clothing Factory and the Tiande Road Rongchangxiang Military Clothing Factory, which did not have adequate fire prevention equipment. The suffering of the victims is deeply felt by those who have witnessed it. It is deeply felt that employees in factories and shops with inadequate fire prevention equipment are everywhere at risk of death. It cannot be denied that all factories in the city are simplifying fire prevention due to their simple and crude conditions, and there are even more people who disregard the lives of their workers for the sake of saving money and have no preparations at all. Once a fire occurs, it cannot be stopped, and it is bound to cause all the workers to be buried in the fire. Even in stores, after closing the market, they must tightly lock the traffic doors and windows, and the key is in the hands of one person. The employer believes that this is enough to prevent theft and prevent employees from going out. If a sudden change occurs, the key holder may lose consciousness due to shock, or be the first to be harmed and lose the key. The door cannot be opened, and there is no way to escape. The lives of those living together will inevitably perish together. Thinking of this, I cannot help but shudder. Therefore, I venture to represent the workers and ask for instructions from the Bureau, requesting that you have mercy and severely crack down on the above-mentioned factories and shops, ordering them to improve. Before complying with the order to improve, order each employer to be responsible for protecting the safety of the employees, in order to maintain life and prevent danger.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests Re-examination and Reduction of Import Tax on Cowhide

Telegram to the Ministry of Finance Requesting Maintenance of Overseas Chinese Livelihoods 125

Regarding the import tax on red tanned cowhide, the Chamber of Commerce has twice requested a reduction, as reported in various newspapers. However, after a considerable time, no definitive announcement has been received from the Ministry of Finance. The Chamber of Commerce believes that the increase or decrease of this tax rate is related to the livelihoods of overseas Chinese and has therefore submitted another petition to the Ministry of Finance, stating: "To the esteemed Nanjing Ministry of Finance: This association, based on the second request from the local Red Tanned Cowhide Trade Association, telegraphed your ministry on September 25th, requesting that the import tax rate on red tanned cowhide from Southeast Asia be promptly reduced. On October 13th, your ministry responded with notification number 11139, acknowledging receipt of the telegram and stating that the matter concerned the revision of tariff regulations, and had previously been forwarded to the National Tariff Commission for consideration. Now that the period for revising import tariffs has arrived, amendments should be awaited as the commission comprehensively considers and finalizes them. The request for prompt reduction is difficult to comply with, etc. After the association recorded this response, it was forwarded. On the 5th of this month, a letter was received from the Singapore Chinese Chamber of Commerce stating: 'Red tanned cowhide is a crucial business for overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia. In recent years, due to the sudden increase in import tax rates by our national customs, which is unfair, sales have been rejected by European and American goods, resulting in significant losses. Many leather factories have already declared closure. Not only are many overseas Chinese merchants unemployed, but even more overseas Chinese laborers are out of work. At a time when rubber and tin mining in our port have repeatedly failed and all industries are declining, how can we further add to the unemployment caused by red tanned cowhide? The unemployment in this industry will not only lead to the decline of the leather industry in our port but also cause our counterparts in your port to suffer the same hardship. To maintain domestic and foreign trade, our chamber has submitted a petition through the resident Tang Consul in Singapore to the national government to revise the import tax rate on red tanned cowhide. Now, according to a letter from your Red Tanned Cowhide Trade Association, we are grateful for your concern for commerce and deep consideration for overseas Chinese affairs, and have already jointly petitioned the Ministry of Finance to revise the tax rate, etc. Upon hearing this, we are filled with admiration. Our chamber, on behalf of all manufacturers in our port's red tanned cowhide industry, expresses our sincere gratitude to your association. Aside from sending a letter requesting your Red Tanned Cowhide Trade Association to prepare samples and submit them to the Jianghai Customs for examination, we believe that if the tax rate is not revised, the leather factories in our port will not be able to resume operations for even a single day, and your leather industry counterparts in your port will also suffer losses every day. This situation greatly impacts domestic and foreign trade. We hope your association will sympathize with overseas Chinese and make a thorough effort to urge our national government to approve the revision of the import tax rate on red tanned cowhide in the shortest possible time so that the leather factories in our port and your leather industry counterparts can resume operations. This is our earnest hope, etc.' Considering that in British Singapore, following the restriction of rubber and tin mining production, countless overseas Chinese businesses have gone bankrupt, and the number of overseas Chinese laborers returning to China is increasing daily, while British territories have restrictions on immigration, our country, which has always relied on the islands of Southeast Asia as an overseas colony, is now on the verge of failure. The chamber's urgent request to reduce the import tax rate on red tanned cowhide to allow the factories to resume operations is indeed a crucial plan to maintain the livelihoods of overseas Chinese. Using the import of silkworm cocoons as an example, the Ministry of Finance reduced the import tariff rate from 12.5% to 7.5% with a ministerial order informing the customs to implement it, without first submitting it to the National Tariff Commission for review. Therefore, there is precedent for the chamber's request for a swift revision. Moreover, the National Tariff Commission's draft for revising import tariffs is rumored to have been prepared long ago and submitted to the Legislative Yuan for passage, lacking only the formality of being promulgated by the National Government. The ministry's instruction, stating that it has already been forwarded to the National Tariff Commission, leaves doubt as to whether the commission has adopted the industry's suggestions and included them in the draft submitted to the Legislative Yuan, as no clear announcement has been made. Based on the aforementioned circumstances, we jointly telegraphed your ministry again to request your careful review and swift remedial measures, providing a detailed reply to alleviate the industry's dire situation, for the public good."

Sun Kui-fang Provides a Detailed Account of the Examination Process in the Xuan A-xiang Case

No Negligence in Self-Adjustment of Duties 126

According to the Guomin She, the Xuan A-xiang case has recently attracted considerable attention in Shanghai. Here, Mr. Sun Kui-fang, Director of the Preparatory Office of the Forensic Examination Institute of the Ministry of Justice, provides a detailed account of the true facts of the examination as follows:

The Nature and Responsibility of Forensic Medicine 127

Recently, various newspapers in Shanghai have published reports on the forensic examination in the Xuan A-xiang case that are largely inaccurate. There are also various misunderstandings about Mr. Kui-fang personally and the Forensic Examination Office. In our country, where forensic medicine is not yet well-developed, inaccurate reports are not surprising, and personal defamation is not worth arguing about. However, I believe that the development of forensic medicine in our country is just beginning. The authorities are determined to improve it and are establishing a forensic research institute in Zhenru to lay the foundation for the future development of forensic medicine. If society loses faith in forensic medicine from the outset, it will have a significant impact on the future of judicial reform. Therefore, I do not hesitate to be tedious in providing a detailed account of the examination process in this case so that those who understand forensic medicine can make appropriate criticisms, and those who do not understand forensic medicine will not be too ignorant of the truth. The transmission of a new academic discipline and the rise of a new career inevitably face considerable resistance. Even in the case of ordinary medicine, the influence of Western medicine in the country today is still far below that of traditional medicine. Furthermore, the introduction of forensic medicine has been even more delayed, and it is not surprising that there are many doubts and confusions. It is hoped that members of society will make calm judgments based on factual evidence and not be swayed by rumors and gossip so that the future of judicial reform will not be excessively hindered, and our country's examination affairs will not be dominated by the "Washed Grievances" and the coroner system for a long time. Scientific research places the utmost importance on evidence.

Forensic methods also focus on physical evidence. From physical evidence, the cause of death can be inferred. However, the same cause of death can be achieved through various actions and methods. What is the true act or method that caused the injury or death? It is necessary to refer to the testimony of witnesses and material evidence outside the body to determine this. For example, if the actions and facts presented by the witness can lead to the cause of death determined by the appraisal and can explain the characteristics of each part of the body without contradiction, the forensic doctor can explain that the evidence is reasonable. However, it cannot be said to be absolutely true because the truthfulness of evidence outside the body is the responsibility of the person in charge of investigation and appraisal and is not within the scope of the forensic doctor's jurisdiction. However, if it is consistent with various characteristics, it is sufficient to constitute extremely strong evidence. Conversely, if the circumstances presented by the witness cannot constitute the cause of death identified by the forensic doctor, the forensic doctor must assume that there are other actions to make a reasonable explanation. As for the existence or absence of other actions, the evidence must be based on: first, the phenomena on the body to determine the cause of death, which is entirely within the scope of the forensic doctor; and second, the integration of evidence outside the body obtained in court with the characteristics examined on the body to infer a reasonable explanation for the cause of death. This is not entirely within the scope of the forensic doctor because the investigation and collection of other evidence outside the body are not within the forensic doctor's duties. The forensic doctor can only determine whether this evidence can be connected with the cause of death and provide an explanation to provide the court with a reference and the investigation with a guideline. If there are unknown facts in the initial investigation of the court, and therefore the cause of death cannot be explained, the forensic doctor has no choice but to speculate that there are other actions besides the evidence. When new facts are discovered that can lead to the cause of death and there are no other actions sufficient to constitute the cause of death as evidence to the contrary, the forensic doctor can change his explanation based on the newly obtained facts. However, as long as the cause of death is not mistaken, the forensic doctor's appraisal cannot be said to be wrong because the forensic doctor cannot anticipate the discovery of new evidence by the court and provide an explanation in advance. Before there is new evidence, it is necessary to make other reasonable explanations. There is also a famous case in forensic medicine that is sufficient to clarify the position of forensic medicine. The knife marks of suicide and homicide usually have obvious distinctions. Suicide knife marks are oblique, running from top to bottom, with the direction being from left to right. This is a common characteristic. Someone once died in a bedroom. The mark on his neck was exactly the same as this. From the perspective of forensic medicine, it is most appropriate to interpret it as suicide. Therefore, the forensic doctor at the time made this appraisal first. After further detailed investigation, it was found that the fingerprints on the knife did not match the deceased's fingerprints, and the distance between the knife and the body was too far, which was also suspicious. Therefore, the investigators, based on the fingerprints, investigated the murderer and were fortunate enough to capture him. When asked about the circumstances of the murder, it turned out that the victim was bowing his head in front, and the murderer bent over behind him to kill him. The state of the injury was completely similar to suicide. Therefore, the forensic doctor had to change his explanation. However, this kind of two-way explanation before and after would not damage the value of forensic medicine but rather increase its reputation. Therefore, the change of explanation is not a problem. The only thing that matters is that the appraisal of the cause of death is consistent with the phenomenon.

The Examination and Process of the Xuan A-xiang Case 128

Now that the nature of forensic medicine and its responsibilities are clear, we can proceed to describe the examination process in the Xuan A-xiang case. However, before describing these facts, there are still some procedures that must be briefly mentioned. During foreign forensic examinations, the court submits the records of the prosecutor's investigation and witness statements to the forensic doctor so that the physical evidence can be compared with this evidence to determine the cause of death and identify whether other evidence is reliable. Because the Shanghai Special District Local Court did not have its own examination site and because of time constraints, it could not be handled in this way. The daily procedure was that in the morning, each police station sent the application forms for court examination to the court. The prosecutor and forensic doctor reviewed the forms one by one and then went to the Yishi Institute of the Public Concession on Fielun Road to examine the bodies. Because of time constraints, after the prosecutor briefly inspected the body, he held a court session to question the witnesses, while the forensic doctor stayed in the examination room to examine the body. Therefore, the forensic doctor's preliminary appraisal was based on the body as physical evidence. As for other circumstances, he could only tentatively rely on the information reported by the police station. The examination of the Xuan A-xiang case was no exception to this procedure. First, the original text of the police station report is recorded below: (Xuan A-xiang, an 18-year-old female, died suddenly at 1:40 pm on September 19, 1930. Zhang Xiao-gui, who lives at 421 Taopeng Road, reported that his niece A-xiang died suddenly at 711 Yangshupu Road with her husband Xu A-san.) Note that this is a false report by Qian A-cai Police Station. ) The report claimed that there was a verbal argument on September 18th at 7 PM when her husband hit her head several times. The next morning, her husband said that his wife (the deceased) was ill and then sent her to Yangshupu Hospital by car. She died before arriving at the hospital. The body was sent to the examination center to await examination. September 20th, Huishan Police Station) The above is the evidence outside the body. Now let's talk about the examination of the body. (1) External examination: Initially, the external examination immediately noted a bloodstain on the left cheekbone of Qian Xuan, with two ridges imprinted on it. However, this was not sufficient to cause death. The prosecutor asked the witness whether she had taken opium. Whether the deceased died from taking opium or whether there was another cause of death could not be determined by external examination and could not be clarified without an autopsy. Therefore, an autopsy was performed. (2) Autopsy: The autopsy originally focused on opium poisoning. Unexpectedly, after opening the chest and abdomen, multiple bleeding spots were found on the lower part of the front of the left and right lungs, which were signs of suffocation. Therefore, suspicion began. The two lungs were taken out one after the other, and the bleeding spots on the lower part of the back were more numerous than those on the front. There were also multiple bleeding spots on the pleura. The heart was opened, and several bleeding spots were found in it, and there was a blood clot in the heart. These bleeding spots, also known as Tardieu's spots, are a unique phenomenon caused by death due to suffocation. The causes of death due to suffocation are mostly due to blockage of the throat tube, except for several diseases. After the phenomenon of suffocation was discovered, the neck had to be searched. After opening the neck skin, blood clots were also found in the muscles of the two major neck tendons, but the outer skin was not injured. Therefore, these blood clots could not but be suspected of being caused by a soft, thick object wrapped around the neck and pressed hard, resulting in internal injury. After opening the scalp, there were round and square bruises inside the scalp. These bruises were also injuries sustained before death. Combining the above external examination and internal autopsy results, there were the following points: (1) There were bloodstains on the face with ridges imprinted on them. (2) The head was injured before death with bruises inside. (3) There were obvious signs of death due to suffocation inside the heart and lungs. (4) There were also bleeding spots in the muscles inside the neck. Combining these points with the information reported by the police station, it could not but be suspected that the deceased was pressed on a table or bed by someone, with her head wrapped in something, and her neck was forcibly suppressed, resulting in death due to suffocation. At the same time, blood vessel dilation and bleeding of the inner lining of the stomach were also found in the stomach (this phenomenon is the same as that found in those who take opium), and the witness also testified that she had taken opium when the prosecutor questioned her. Therefore, the contents of the stomach had to be chemically examined to complete the examination procedure. However, our country's courts do not have drug testing equipment and have to rely on the Public Concession Health Department for chemical examination. What was requested from the Public Concession Health Department was the result of chemical examination, not an opinion on the cause of death, because no one who has not seen the entire examination can determine that death was necessarily caused by the presence of toxic substances in the stomach. It should be noted that the various signs of suffocation mentioned above were not all caused by ordinary opium poisoning, but were entirely signs of suffocation. Even without the ingestion of opium, this suffocation would undoubtedly be sufficient to constitute the cause of death. Since the above cause of death was determined, the Public Concession Health Department was commissioned to test for poison for reference, and the cause of death was explained first. This is the text of the explanation in the first examination report (the bloodstains on her left cheekbone) were caused by someone pressing hard on the back of her head, injuring her face. Her face also touched objects with sharp edges (bed boards or edges), so there were ridge imprints. The bruises on the left side of her hairline and to the left were caused by rectangular blunt objects and punches. The blood clots in the muscles on both sides of her neck (sternocleidomastoid muscles) (i.e., the two major neck tendons) were caused by the perpetrator pressing on both sides of her neck with his hands. There was something padded on the outside (such as a blanket), so there were no injuries on the outer skin, but there were blood clots inside. The bleeding spots on her lungs, heart, and other organs were a unique phenomenon caused by death due to suffocation. According to the above situation, it seems that the perpetrator wrapped the victim's head and body with something like a blanket and also used blunt objects and punches on her head, pressing hard on the back of the victim's head, causing a large bloodstain on the left cheekbone of her upper part, and the ridge of the padding penetrated the skin. There were multiple blood clots in the sternocleidomastoid muscles of her neck, indicating that the perpetrator had pressed hard on the victim's neck, causing the trachea to be blocked, and the victim died due to suffocation. Therefore, there were bleeding spots on her lungs, heart, and other organs. Furthermore, it should be added that Mr. Kui-fang's task in Shanghai was to establish a forensic research institute (formerly the Forensic Examination Office) under the order of the Ministry. To examine cases of body examinations and injuries for the special district local court was to act under commission. Preparing for this required traveling back and forth between Beijing and Shanghai, which took a considerable amount of time, and the local court had to deal with many cases of body examinations and injuries every day. Therefore, although every effort was made to deliver the examination reports quickly, there were occasional delays due to other matters. However, there were never any delays that went unexamined, as reported in the newspapers. (3) Drug testing results: Although the above explanation can explain the cause of death, since there was drug use, a drug test had to be performed at the same time to complete the procedure. Therefore, the stomach was taken out, along with several small pieces of other internal organs and urine, and entrusted to the Public Concession Health Department for examination. The task of the department in this matter was only to report on the results on the certificate and could not express an opinion on the cause of death. Since the entire examination was not known, only finding that there was opium poison could not be used to determine the cause of death, and they were never entrusted to make this assessment. Moreover, determining whether there was poison or not does not require any profound technology, but the Health Department has this equipment. Later, the Health Department's drug testing form only stated that opium poison was found in the stomach and urine. When this form was sent over, Mr. Kui-fang happened to be in Beijing for business, and his colleague in the forensic laboratory sent the testing form to the Prosecutor's Office. After Mr. Kui-fang returned to Shanghai, Judge Feng Shi-de asked whether it could be explained as death due to drug use, as the testing form stated that the stomach and urine contained opium. Mr. Kui-fang replied that although the chemical testing results showed the presence of opium poison, death solely from drug use would not cause the bruises and bleeding spots on the face, head, and internal organs. Before the opium poison took effect, the deceased may have been injured by someone. Therefore, unless there is other evidence sufficient to explain the various phenomena mentioned above, from the forensic point of view, it still cannot be said to be solely death due to drug use. (4) New evidence and second explanation: Judge Feng then stated that, according to the witness's testimony, Xuan A-xiang had been lying on the table since the evening of the 19th until the next morning, and that she was still lying on the table (this statement was not mentioned when the prosecutor questioned her before). Moreover, no other evidence was obtained in court to prove that the deceased died of forcible suffocation. The court could not obtain evidence for the first speculative explanation from afar, but the fact that she was lying on the table could provide a reasonable explanation for the marks on her face and the phenomenon of death due to suffocation. Therefore, based on the circumstances, a second explanation was made as follows: (hereinafter the original text) According to the drug testing certificate issued by the Public Concession Health Department, the stomach fluid and urine of Xuan A-xiang contained a large amount of opium. According to the statements of the witness and the defendant, Xuan A-xiang had an argument with her husband the day before her death, and when she returned home that night, she lay on the table until dawn. Therefore, according to the report of the Public Concession and the statements of the witness and the defendant, the injuries and cause of death described in the examination report of September 25 should be explained separately. The bloodstains on her left cheekbone were caused by the deceased gradually losing her self-control after taking opium, which caused her to rub her face against the table, thus injuring her cheekbone, and the edge of the table penetrated the skin. The blood clots in the sternocleidomastoid muscles of her neck were caused by her head tilting from side to side after losing her self-control, which caused the muscles to stretch beyond their limit, thus there was bleeding in the muscles. The state of death due to suffocation internally was also caused by her covering her mouth and nose with her sleeves after losing her self-control, and she eventually died of suffocation, so there were bleeding spots in the internal organs and lungs. As for the wounds on her head, they were still caused by others before her death. From the above process, it can be seen that the explanations before and after are based on the same cause of death. The first explanation was because the fact that she was lying on the table was unknown, and death solely from drug use could not have caused the aforementioned phenomena. Moreover, the deceased died due to marital discord, so the most recent speculation had to be made, suspecting that there was forcible suffocation. The second explanation was because the forensic doctor did not obtain actual evidence for the first speculation, and the fact that she was lying on the table could explain the phenomena on the body, so it was okay to change it. The difference between the explanations before and after came from evidence outside the body and was not caused by errors in the body examination. The scope of the forensic doctor's responsibilities is limited to showing the court the direction for searching for evidence based on the phenomena of the body, and seeking an understandable explanation by referring to the evidence obtained by the court and the condition of the body. The forensic doctor's responsibilities are limited to this, and it is not within the forensic doctor's jurisdiction to investigate how to search for external evidence and whether it is true or false, detailed or rough. Moreover, in the special circumstances in which Mr. Kui-fang was in, he had no time to ask about it. However, because his first explanation was able to come up with the fact that she was lying on the table, he was fortunate that he had not made any major negligence in his duties. In short, the spirit of forensic medicine is to obtain results from empirical evidence. It cannot prematurely predict facts, nor can it recklessly determine the cause of death regardless of evidence. Although the deceased took opium, if her special posture at the time of death was not sufficient to explain the evidence obtained, a conclusion could not be drawn rashly. All scientific progress is based on the spirit of seeking evidence, and forensic medicine cannot be an exception. As for whether society can understand this, it depends on how well society understands this spirit.

In addition, there are two other matters involving individuals recorded in the newspapers. One is the case of the mentally ill Gua Hu Zhang. This matter is due to the difference between criminal appraisal and ordinary appraisal. I still believe that the appraisal made has never been wrong. Since it involves expertise, it is not necessary to argue about it here. I plan to comment on it in court. What I hope from the people of the country is not to regard the appraisal of the Public Concession as too important and to regard the appraisal of the people of our country as too unimportant. This kind of mentality seems to be temporarily difficult to change in our country, especially in Shanghai, but in the future, there may eventually be a time when they realize their mistake. There is also a matter that Mr. Kui-fang received a large amount of money to travel abroad, and the Shanghai Forensic Examination Office disappeared without a trace. The truth or falsehood of these rumors can be verified by facts, and it is not necessary to argue about them deeply. I only wish to point out that my trip abroad was under the order of the Ministry, and the temporary relocation of the Forensic Examination Preparation Office to Nanjing was also based on the order of the Ministry. The reason for the delay in replying to the newspaper reports this time was that I was preparing for departure procedures in Beijing. Fortunately, I have not started my journey yet, and I can still have the opportunity to answer these rumors. However, as I am about to leave for the West, if there are any more criticisms against individuals, I will have to wait until I return to defend myself. I hereby declare this to avoid misunderstandings.

Local News Two

Yellow Croaker Case Trial Record 132

Plaintiff Received Anonymous Letter

Threatening That a Peaceful Settlement Is Required

There Was a Contract for Selling Yellow Croaker

The Debate Concluded, Awaiting Judgment

Wang Fucai from Ningbo, an employee of the American merchant ship *SS Chefoo*, invited his colleague Li Zaichen to Room 13 of the Ningbo Hotel on Dongxinqiao Street in the French Concession on the evening of the 30th of last month, where he demanded 4,000 yuan from Li under false pretenses. The case was uncovered and Wang, along with a suspect named Xu Lihui from Ningbo, was arrested by Chinese detectives Liu Junjie, Shen Dehui, Feng Qi, etc., from the Hongkou Police Station and sent to the Special District Court for questioning. Wang was remanded in custody, and Xu was released on bail of 1,000 yuan pending further investigation. This newspaper reported on this case the day before yesterday. Presiding Judge Ge Zhitian held a continued hearing in court. According to Zhang Tianyin, a lawyer from the police station, during the adjournment, the plaintiff received an anonymous letter stating that the case must be settled peacefully, otherwise there would be unfavorable consequences. The letter was submitted as evidence. The defendant's representative, lawyer Fan Gang, also submitted a contract, stating that the contract was between the plaintiff and the now-defunct heads Zhao Xiuqing and Yang Fucai, for a joint venture of smuggling yellow croaker, which could prove that the plaintiff was accustomed to doing this kind of thing. The plaintiff, Li Zaichen, testified that the contract was not written by him. In March, the former cook heads Yang Fugui, Wang Fucai, and four others smuggled a batch of yellow croaker and asked for my help. The passenger disembarked in Singapore, but was discovered by customs officers at the Italian Wharf and deported ashore. After the ship returned to Shanghai, Yang was dismissed by the Western shipowner, and Wang took over. This time, 18 yellow croakers were smuggled, and I did not receive a single penny, so I reported the arrest and detained the two defendants. Judge Ge had Li write a paper based on the wording of the contract, carefully examined the handwriting, and kept it on file. Xia Shunlai testified that he was the general manager of Chinese affairs for the *SS Chefoo* company. Li Zaichen and Wang Fucai were both hired by me on behalf of the company as heads on the ship. On the 30th of last month, I was in Room 99 of the Dadong Hotel on Nanjing Road because I was ordered by the Western shipowner to replace all the heads, workers, and servants on the ship, a total of more than 30 people, with new ones. Li Zaichen and Wang Fucai arrived one after the other, and soon left. I didn't know anything about their going to the Ningbo Hotel to settle the yellow croaker account. Yang Ahua testified that he helped Wang Fucai as a stoker. This time, the private smuggling of yellow croaker was a joint venture by the plaintiff Li Zaichen, Wang Fucai, and Zhao Xiuqing, totaling US$1,450. This time, Li was the leader, and he said that the distribution of the profits to us assistants would be at their discretion. Questioned, Wang Fucai insisted that the plaintiff and Zhao Xiuqing, Yang Fugui, etc., had signed a contract for private smuggling of yellow croaker, saying that they would share the blessings and share the burdens, but he did not know who wrote the contract. He only knew that he and the plaintiff were actually in the Ningbo Hotel to settle the account for the American yellow croaker they smuggled together. This time, no contract was signed, and the money would be distributed to more than 30 colleagues on the ship after it was obtained. He pointed to the plaintiff and said, "You swallowed this money, your conscience is too black. If you want to prosecute me again, I will report it to your children and grandchildren." When questioned, Xu Lihui firmly denied demanding money from the plaintiff and did not know anything about the yellow croaker smuggling, asking for an investigation. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stood up again and said that according to the special provisions of the US immigration law, although there is no imprisonment, there should be a fine. Because the cost of living in that country is quite high, an American worker's daily wage must be US$4 or 5. If a Chinese person goes to the US, he is willing to accept US$1 or 2 per day, so the US authorities established an immigration bureau to help the country's unemployed workers. Each Chinese is sent back to his country. According to the defendants, the cost of sending each person back is US$1,450, so the plaintiff should get more than 38,000 yuan. Judge Ge ordered the lawyers on both sides to begin the debate. After a while, he ordered the defendant Wang Fucai to be remanded in custody, and Xu Lihui to continue to be released on bail pending the scheduled judgment.

Yu Yunqing Sues

Wife Fled, Unbearable Cohabitation 133

Yu is 59 Years Old

His Wife is 42 Years Old

The Children Have Grown Up

But He Firmly Requests a Divorce

Yu Yunqing from Songjiang has filed a lawsuit in the local court against his wife, Ms. Shen, for deserting him and living away from home for a long time, making cohabitation unbearable. He requests a divorce. His statement is roughly as follows: The plaintiff is 59 years old, a native of Songjiang, and currently lives at No. 43 Fumin Road, Dananmen. He married Ms. Shen (42 years old this year) in the 34th year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty. At first, they lived peacefully and had one son and one daughter each (son named Deng'ao, 18 years old, daughter named Yingu, 22 years old), who are both of marriageable age. Since the 7th year of the Republic of China, the defendant has been degenerating, often associating with hooligans. In the 12th year of the Republic of China, she fled without a trace, taking away a pair of gold bracelets and a suitcase. At that time, a report was filed with the police, but there was no progress. The defendant took advantage of the plaintiff's service in the store and brought four or five hooligans into the plaintiff's home and took away a leather suitcase, clothes, silver dollars, etc., totaling more than a thousand gold. The defendant is unwilling to be a couple with the plaintiff and has been gone for seven years, abandoning the plaintiff as if he were a stranger. Is her intention still questionable? If a formal divorce is not declared, I am afraid of being entangled endlessly. Judge Dong Tong held a hearing and the plaintiff testified to the previous situation, saying that he had now remarried a woman named Li from Hangzhou, because Ms. Shen did not observe the virtues of a woman and had an affair with my cousin, and soon became acquainted with others. The defendant's address is unknown, so she could not be served with a summons and did not appear. The specially appointed lawyer Chen Kuitang appeared in court to object, saying that since the children have grown up, they should come to court to testify. The official instructed the plaintiff to bring his children to court next time to be questioned. Yesterday, the court convened again at 10 a.m. and was presided over by Judge Tong Shenglu in the Ninth Tribunal. The plaintiff Yu Yunqing gave a brief account of the previous situation. When questioned, Yu Deng'ao testified that my mother left around the 9th or 10th year of the Republic of China. Lawyer Chen stated that the plaintiff's complaint stated that the defendant fled in the 12th year of the Republic of China, but his son said that it was around the 9th or 10th year. There is an obvious discrepancy in the details. The defendant may be in Shanghai, but the plaintiff has not conducted a thorough investigation. Moreover, the children born to the defendant have all grown up. If the defendant has committed the seven grounds for divorce, there are still three reasons for not divorcing. Either she has seen the parents-in-law through their old age and burial, or she has nowhere else to go. He asked the court to pay attention. The presiding judge ordered that the matter be verified and handled.

Aunt Sues Widow

Seeking Separation of Family Relationship 134

The Daughter-in-Law Was Caught in Adultery

During the Trial, the Daughter-in-Law Insisted That She Was Framed

Debate Concluded, Judgment on the 11th

Gao Caijun from Taixian, who opened a rice store at No. 27 Taiyangmiao, Zhabei, died in the 15th year of the Republic of China, leaving behind his wife, Gao Zhang (29 years old), who observed the virtues of a woman. In September of this year, she brought her lover, Feng Yutang, to her home for a secret meeting, when she was reported to the police by Gao Caibei (the husband's younger brother). Feng and Ms. Gao were arrested and taken to the prosecutor's office of the District Court. After the prosecutor questioned them, he dismissed the case and released Feng on bail. Ms. Gao Zhang was also released. After being released, Gao Zhang filed a lawsuit in the civil court of the District Court, demanding that her husband's younger brother, Gao Caibei, distribute the property (about 10,000 gold, divided into two shares). After hearing the case, it was rejected. Now, Gao Lu, the aunt of Gao Zhang, has hired lawyer Ye Fukang to file a lawsuit in the District Court, requesting to separate from her daughter-in-law Gao Zhang. Her statement is roughly as follows: The defendant Gao Zhang has committed adultery, which has damaged the reputation of the family. The defendant is the plaintiff's daughter-in-law. Since her son's death, she has been restless, and people have been gossiping. At first, there was no evidence, but on the night of the 18th of September of this year, at 1:00 a.m., Feng Yutang blatantly broke into the daughter-in-law's room for a secret meeting. The plaintiff's second son, Caibei, suddenly heard a loud noise coming from the defendant's room, so he reported it to the police, who broke in and arrested the defendant and Feng together and transferred them to the Fourth District Bureau, which then transferred them to your court's prosecutor's office. After investigating, the defendant's adultery has harmed public morals. Therefore, I request to separate from her. The defendant Gao Zhang also hired lawyer Yan Lunkui to present a defense, saying that the plaintiff's complaint has no basis and that a news report in the newspaper is the only reliable evidence. The defendant is completely pure and self-respecting and has never had any improper behavior. Even if she had improper behavior, as the plaintiff said, she had an affair with Feng Yutang. Can a newspaper report be used as evidence? The defendant was brought to the Gao family as a child bride by her father, Zhang Buhua, when she was eight years old. When she grew up, she married Gao Caijun, the eldest son of Gao Lu. Caijun died at the age of 26. It has been four years since then. If the defendant is really a born slut and can sleep with anyone, then the scandal should have spread long ago. Moreover, Feng Yutang is a close friend of her husband's younger brother, Gao Caibei, and is also the godfather of Caibei's daughter, Xiaomaotou. Therefore, Feng once confessed that he was actually instigated by Caibei to seduce the defendant and force her to marry him. In the plaintiff's original complaint, she said that a chaste widow is legally entitled to inherit her husband's share, which means that she has no regard for the son of the deceased (the son of the deceased is five years old) and only recognizes that the widow has the right to inherit her husband's share. Is it not enough to slander her with adultery to seize the widow's share of the property? If she can harm an adult widow today, it is hard to guarantee that she will not harm a minor orphan in the future. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang Keqian opened the Fourth Tribunal to hear the case. Both parties came with their lawyers. The plaintiff Gao Lu gave an account of the matter. (Question) Have you ever reconciled outside of court? (Answer) I agreed to give 300 yuan, but the defendant wanted 700 yuan, so it was not resolved. The judge ordered the defendant Gao Zhang to deny the adultery in the case. The judge said, "If you didn't have an affair with Feng Yutang, how could you have Feng's clothes in your room?" The former prosecutor did not prosecute because your husband was dead, so adultery was not established. The defendant insisted that she was framed. "My husband had a share of the family property, and I want to live with my son. I never said I wanted 700 yuan. The plaintiff asked someone to say to me to give me 800 yuan, but I didn't agree." At this point, the plaintiff's lawyer stood up and said that Feng Yutang was caught naked at the time and confessed that he had been having an affair for three years. The defendant said that the plaintiff had a great intention to plot for money. Then the debate began, and the judge considered the conclusion to be set for judgment at 2:00 p.m. on the 11th of this month.

Various Fellow Associations

Publish Declaration on the Xin Case 135

*Riri News* reports that various fellow provincial associations in Shanghai yesterday issued a declaration on the case of Xin Dingxiang, stating: (In recent years, our Chinese people have often been slaughtered by imperialists. The major cases include the Shaji Massacre, the Wanzhou Incident, the May Thirtieth Movement, and the May Third Incident. The humiliation and shame are deeply known to the Chinese people. As for the individuals who have been slaughtered, they either endure it in silence or are not valued by the Chinese people. However, counting on our fingers, there are countless cases that are obvious to everyone. If we have any spirit, we must think about it calmly and feel angry and indignant. Although the reasons for causing these tragic cases are what? In a word, it is the lack of diplomacy in a weak country. The imperialists use unequal treaties as a talisman and treat the Chinese people as if they are invisible, especially the working-class friends who earn their living by their own labor. They are regarded as sacrifices under the iron hooves. Not only do they treat us as subordinate colonies, but they also treat the people of our dignified Republic of China as inferior to grass and dogs. The old humiliation has not yet been washed away, and new humiliation is being added. The recent case of French sailors killing our compatriot Xin Dingxiang is particularly hateful. This kind of brutal behavior is actually done by people who claim to be civilized countries, which is a blatant exposure of their hideous faces. We should know that the occurrence of the Xin case is not only a personal problem, but a matter of life and death for the entire nation. The more we come into contact with imperialists, the more we are in danger of losing our lives. A rabbit dies, and a fox mourns; things hurt their own kind. How can we stand idly by when it involves the national system? Our associations are deeply indignant about this tragic case for the sake of humanity and the survival of the nation. After a joint meeting, a consensus was reached to fight to awaken the imperialists and to be pioneers in popular diplomacy. The minimum requirements must be achieved: punish the murderers, compensate, apologize, and guarantee that similar incidents will not happen again. The police officers who privately released the murderers must be severely punished, and the foreign troops stationed in China must be withdrawn, the unequal treaties must be abolished, and the concessions must be recovered without delay. We will fight to the end and will never give up until we achieve our goals. We dare to lead the fellow villagers in Shanghai to provide strong support for the Xin case, and we hope that the people of the country will rise up to help. The country is fortunate, and the nation is fortunate. This is our declaration. Ningbo Fellow Association, Pinghu Fellow Association, Huining Fellow Association, Suzhou Fellow Association, Dapu Fellow Association, Fenghua Fellow Association, Dongshan Fellow Association, Jiangning Fellow Association, Danyang Fellow Association, Shaoxing Fellow Association, Dinghai Fellow Association, Xiaoshan Fellow Association, Wenzhou Fellow Association, Fujian Fellow Association, Xuzhou Fellow Association, Tongru Chonghai Fellow Association, Anhui Fellow Association, Hubei Fellow Association, Hunan Fellow Association, Guangzhao Association, Jiaxing Fellow Association, Huzhou Fellow Association, Huzhou Hunan Fellow Association, Taizhou Fellow Association, Zhenhai Fellow Association, Wuxi Fellow Association, Sanbei Shanghai Fellow Association.

Woman Requests Property Division

Not Yet of Legal Age 140

Should Accompany Mother to Court Next Time

Zhu Xiulan, a local woman, lives in the Nantou area of Pudong. Her father, Zhu Ziqing, died in the 17th year of the Republic of China, and her mother is still alive. There are five siblings: the eldest sister is named Zhang Ying, the second brother is Zengxiang, the third brother is Qingxiang, the fourth sister is Cailan, and the fifth is Xiulan. Now, Xiulan has suddenly hired lawyer Wang Youlin to draft a statement to the District Court, suing her brothers Zengxiang and Qingxiang for seizing the property and not dividing it, and requesting a division of the inheritance. Her intention to sue is that her two brothers have married and her two sisters have married, so all of her late father Ziqing's inheritance should be divided into three shares. Yesterday morning, Judge Tong Shenglu opened a court hearing. The defendants Zhu Zengxiang and Zhu Qingxiang did not attend and instead appointed lawyer Qu Jinwei to represent them. The plaintiff Zhu Xiulan came with lawyer Wang and stated that she was a 20-year-old Shanghainese. (Question) When is your birthday? (Answer) The ninth day of the fourth month, at night. I don't know when I was born. (Question) Have you ever been married? (Answer) No. (Question) Is your mother still alive? (Answer) My father has passed away, but my mother, Zhu Yan, is still alive. The official said, "You are not of legal age to sue. Your mother should come out to make a claim. According to the law, you must be 20 years old, but you will not be 20 years old until the ninth day of the fourth month of next year, after your birthday." At this point, the defendant's lawyer stood up and said, "After investigating, this inheritance has already been divided and the relatives were present at the scene. 3 mu, 6 li, and 7 hao of land in the 24th Bao and 15th Tu of Shangyi have been distributed to the plaintiff. This time, the plaintiff's lawsuit has no basis and should be dismissed." The judge then said to the plaintiff, "You should accompany your mother to court next time. It would be best to reconcile out of court to avoid hurting the feelings between siblings." After the order, the court adjourned.

The Two Newlyweds Were Greatly Frightened 141

The Guests Were Also Greatly Disappointed

Mo Rongsheng, a native of Shengqiao Township in western Shanghai, is a mechanic at a yarn factory in Yangshupu, Shanghai. Murder Case in Qujiaqiao, Luodian, Baoshan

The Murderer Qian Xingsheng Was Sentenced to Death 142

The Wife of the Deceased, Zhang Wang, Was Acquitted

Zhou Wang (also known as Zhang Wang, 29 years old), a farmer from Qujiaqiao, Luodian, Baoshan, was a widow. In the spring of this year, she had an affair with Qian Xingsheng (22 years old), a local fisherman. Soon after, Yu Ahua, an ant matchmaker, sold her to the deceased Zhang Shengrong to be his wife. Unexpectedly, on the seventh day after arriving at Zhang's house, Qian Xingsheng, hating Zhang Shengrong for occupying his lover, took a sharp knife on the night of the 16th of last month and climbed down from the roof of Zhang's house. He sneaked into Zhang's bedroom and, taking advantage of Zhang and Wang sleeping soundly, stabbed Zhang in the throat and right under the throat with the sharp knife, penetrating about seven inches. Zhang died instantly. Qian then fled. When Wang woke up, she touched her clothes in the dark and found that they were very wet and smelled of blood. She called out to Zhang, but there was no response. Then, she woke up Zhang Ajin, the uncle who lived with them, and lit a fire to see that Zhang had already died. Then, she informed Zhang's father, Tingjue, of the situation and immediately went to the third sub-bureau of the Public Security Bureau to report the incident. After Bureau Chief Gao Xitian repeatedly questioned Wang about the identity of the murderer, she said that she suspected it was her former lover, Qian Xingsheng. After receiving the report, the bureau immediately sent police officers to arrest Qian. Qian Xingsheng refused to be arrested and fled. In the end, he was not caught due to the darkness. The next day, the bureau prepared a document and reported it to the General Bureau, which then reported it to the county government for an autopsy. Subsequently, the Public Security Bureau arrested the murderer Qian Xingsheng and sent him to the county government. County Chief Qiu Mingjiu repeatedly sent the investigating officer Huang Jie to hold a court hearing. Qian Xingsheng confessed to the murder, but said that Wang had asked him to kill Zhang Shengrong in the fields on the afternoon of the 22nd and at Yangmuqiao on the morning of the 23rd so that they could resume their old relationship. Wang坚决否认有教唆及帮杀情事继据尸叔张阿金供称该两日均在家中未曾外出等语末据尸父张亭爵供称其子被杀之后系王氏喊醒张阿金由张阿金之子阿宝通知等语是案发生后宝山各界人士大为注意业经审理终结宣判钱杏生预谋杀人一罪处死刑褫夺公权无期周王氏无罪开释 Wang firmly denied that she had instigated or helped with the murder. Zhang Ajin, the uncle of the deceased, testified that he was at home on both of those days and did not go out. Finally, Zhang Tingjue, the father of the deceased, testified that after his son was killed, Wang woke up Zhang Ajin, and Zhang Ajin's son, Abao, notified him. After the case occurred, all sectors of Baoshan paid great attention to it. After the trial was concluded, Qian Xingsheng was sentenced to death for premeditated murder and deprived of his political rights for life. Zhou Wang was acquitted.

The Grand Funeral of Wu Linshu Yesterday 143

The funeral of Mr. Wu Linshu, former manager of Tongyi Yarn Factory, took place yesterday. At nine o'clock in the morning, the procession set off from his residence on Avenue Haig, turned onto Seymour Road, passed Jing'an Temple Road, entered Nanjing Road, went past Jiangxi Road, circled Avenue Edward VII, and proceeded along Xizang Road to Pingjiang Guild Hall on Xinzhapu Road for temporary placement. Ahead of the ceremonial guard were four mounted attendants. At the very front were mounted patrol officers dispatched by the police. Following were about a hundred or so flags and banners of condolence from various sectors. Next was the military band of the Shanghai Poor Children's Home, followed by wreaths from various sectors loaded onto four cars. Behind them came the troops of the French Concession Volunteer Corps and a delegation of female workers from Tongyi Yarn Factory, numbering over two hundred, who were also riding in seven buses of the concession. Following was the entire staff of Tongyi, numbering over a hundred, all dressed in dark blue uniforms.

The Funeral Procession of Mr. Wu Linshu 144

The format was extremely solemn and orderly. Next was the military band of the orphanage. Following closely were about four hundred male workers from Tongyi Yarn Factory, all wearing blue cloth uniforms with a memorial badge for Mr. Wu's funeral pinned on the left breast. The badge had a blue border with a portrait of Mr. Wu in the center, and the words "Mr. Wu Linshu Funeral Memorial" printed on the edge. Nurses from the Pingmin Hospital, riding in four cars, followed closely behind. Next was the hearse with the portrait, led by the Municipal Police Bureau military band, which was renowned throughout Shanghai. Finally, there was the mourning canopy and then the hearse.

Page 12

The military band of the Songhu Garrison Command brought up the rear. There were a total of about seventy cars in the funeral procession, with Yunfei Company cars accounting for fifty of them. Each car was decorated with a black ribbon bow, and the uniform color of the cars added to the extremely quiet and solemn atmosphere. Behind the funeral cars was the company's road-clearing vehicle, taking care of the order along the way. Spectators praised the scene incessantly. When the procession passed through Nanjing Road, north-south traffic on Xizang Road, Zhejiang Road, Fujian Road, Henan Road, and other streets was disrupted for about ten minutes before returning to normal. It is said that among Chinese people whose funerals have been able to pass through Nanjing Road, the first was Sheng Xingzun, the second was Zhu Bao San, and now Mr. Wu ranks third.

Stone Splinter Bursts Into Temple

Wang Fugui Dies Tragically 145

Wang Fugui, a 24-year-old coppersmith from Ningbo working at Sun Qimei Ironworks, No. 30 Linqing Road, Yangshupu, had been working at the factory for several years. He earned one dollar and ten cents per day. Yesterday morning around 9:45, Wang was working on a machine when, unexpectedly, a huge dry whetstone being used on a machine to his left suddenly exploded with a loud bang. A piece about the size of a fist struck Wang squarely in the temple, causing him to fall to the ground in agony and die instantly. People immediately transported him to Tongren Hospital and then to the forensic examination office on Feilun Road for an autopsy.

Chicken Ball Brand Fire Extinguisher Demonstrated Yesterday 146

The Zhendan Chicken Ball Brand Powder Fire Extinguisher, invented by Xue Zhenxiang, owner of Zhendan Machinery Factory, was summoned to the capital on the first of this month by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for a demonstration. Press Association Gathering Soon

Lawyer Bian Jialu Commences Practice 149

Lawyer Bian Jialu formerly worked in the French General Police Station in the city and had a constant interest in studying law. After leaving his post, he devoted himself to the revolution. Once the political situation stabilized, he entered a law school and studied diligently. He graduated this summer and applied to the Ministry of Justice for certification to join the Shanghai Lawyers' Association. He has formed a law firm with the renowned lawyer Yu Zufeng and will practice at No. 39 Avenue Edward VII. He attended a swearing-in ceremony at the French Court the morning before yesterday. Mr. Bian has a profound knowledge of law and is sure to use his knowledge to protect social and human rights.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast yesterday at 4:30 p.m. stated: The Yangtze River basin and coastal areas will be cloudy and cold. There will be strong winds from the northwest to northeast on Shandong and the Yellow Sea. There will be northeast winds south of the Yangtze River estuary. The weather in the Korean Strait is bad due to the low pressure moving to the northeast-east. The hurricane in the southeast of Gamu is clearly turning northwest and advancing. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 p.m. yesterday, the highest temperature in the city was 64.4 and the lowest was 59.7. On the same day last year, the highest was 60.6 and the lowest was 54.9.
