Free Talk

Laugh It Off 154

— Sea Guest

A: I met Miss Ding C on the street today.

B: Did you congratulate her? She's married.

A: I know. It's too late to congratulate her now. I'll wait until she gets divorced and congratulate her then.

Man: You're very rich.

Woman: Yes, my father only had me. I'll inherit 200,000 in the future.

Man: But I have no money.

Woman: Who told you to be born into a poor family?

Man: Would you be willing to marry me?

Woman: How can that be? I want to marry a rich man.

Man: I knew you wouldn't marry me.

Woman: Then why did you propose to me?

Man: I wanted to see how a man would feel if he lost 200,000 gold.

A: I heard you broke up with your fiancée.

B: Yes, because I found something on her that I didn't want to see.

A: What was it?

B: I found her with one of her male classmates, their arms around each other, sitting in the shade of the park.

Wife: You're too unaware, always looking for trouble.

Husband: Yes, that's why I found you that year.

Mr. Hu and the Reading Movement 155

— Yan Qian

Recently, a novel undertaking has emerged in Shanghai society, namely the youth association's reading movement. Yesterday was the first day of the opening, with Mr. Hu Shih giving a lecture on "Why Read?" I will briefly record Mr. Hu's lecture and some interesting details to share with readers of this column.

Those Who Came Late Rushed In When the author arrived at 3:00 p.m., I saw a large crowd gathered in front of the office counter. I went forward to inquire and learned that all the tickets had been distributed and everyone was demanding accommodation. At that time, there were still two hours before the start of the lecture, and those who came were already expressing regret. This shows the sensational nature of the event and the appeal of Mr. Hu. After I arrived, more people continued to arrive until 4:30, so the staff in the meeting were repeatedly surrounded by latecomers. Finally, they defused the situation with the phrase (wait until those with tickets are seated before opening the doors to accommodate the gentlemen who came late). However, many of those who came late were unwilling to wait for a long time and wanted to force their way in. The gatekeepers also firmly refused to let them in, so the crowd of latecomers temporarily united and agreed to charge. For a while, the sounds of (push!) (charge!) never stopped. In the end, they were victorious and rushed into the meeting. Taking advantage of the force of those pushing in front and behind, the author also took the opportunity to enter. At that time, the laughter of victory replaced the sound of effort. This may be a harbinger of the future courage and progress of the reading community.

Three Points on Reading At 5:00, after the singing of the party song, the ceremony, and the silence, Mr. Hu stood up to give his lecture. He first expressed humility, saying that teaching me how to read or what to read is very easy to talk about, but why read is a bit difficult, and I am afraid I will not speak well. Now I will try it. He then said that he had given a lecture on this question once before, and the manuscript happened to be collected in the third volume of Hu Shih's essays. Gentlemen, you may wish to refer to it. Then he entered the subject and said that there are three points in reading: first, books are a record of knowledge, wisdom, and experience, and the heritage of mankind. Reading is to accept this heritage and use it as a foundation to develop and expand it. The second is to read for the sake of reading, because mankind has a need to read, so we read. The more we read, the more books we can read. The third is to read to solve difficulties. When difficulties are present, we must think, and thinking can generate ideas. With ideas, it is good to choose a suitable doctrine to solve the difficulties. If you do not read, you will not have ideas. The more you read, the more ideas you will naturally have, and it will be easier to solve the difficulties. Mr. Hu cited many examples when he spoke, and he was very eloquent, so it took a long time.

Half a Dozen Goods in a Grocery Store Finally, Mr. Hu said again that he had already stated in advance that speaking may encroach on other scheduled topics. Now I want to contribute a little opinion, that is, how do we read? I have read books for 35 years, but these 35 years of experience tell me that very few of the many books in China are systematic and structured. They are all unplanned, casually compiled successes. The so-called Classics, History, Philosophy, and Collections are obviously grocery stores. However, is Philosophy not also a grocery store? Are History and Classics not also grocery stores? Because it is a grocery store, there are very few that are truly systematic and structured. At most, only half a dozen are up to the previous conditions. Therefore, we only read Chinese books and feel that it is not enough, so we must learn at least one foreign language in order to achieve the effect of extensive reading, extensive collection, and analogy. If scholars can put in a year of hard work, not afraid of trouble, look up unfamiliar words, identify sentences, and understand each word and sentence very clearly, they will have good results. If they continue to work hard, there will be a day when you can read foreign books in bed without effort. That is the joy of reading, and the joy is endless. At this point, Mr. Hu bowed and retired in the midst of applause.

Small Suggestions on the Railroad 156

— Yu Qing

Modify Cars with Iron Wheels Use Instead of Special Trains

Every time important people go in and out, special trains are opened. Military

It goes without saying during the period. It is probably because of time constraints that it will delay national affairs. We cannot deeply criticize the authorities for their mistakes. However, the cost of trains is huge and the expenses are considerable. In my opinion, cars can be modified with iron wheels and placed on the railroad, still using the car engine to start. It will run fast and save money. If the cost of each special train is 100 yuan, and the cost of using a car is 10 yuan, this can save 10%. Accumulating a little can also be a major economic avenue.

Record of Shen Li's Marriage 157

— Huang Yingdai

On November 1st, my cousin Shen Dashi, introduced by Dr. Lu Jinhou and Mr. Liu Shumei, married Ms. Li Guoqi, the granddaughter of Li Hanzhang of Hefei, at the Dahua Hotel. A banquet was held at the Xin Xin Restaurant in the evening, and important people came to watch, which was a great event at the time. I will record the interesting things I saw to share with readers of this column.

Solemn and Brilliant Hall More than twenty pairs of flower baskets filled the hall, with silver screens, silver shields, and other objects in the middle. Behind was the music stage, and in front was the guest seating area. When the wedding ceremony was held, the ceiling lights in the hall were all lit up, as if the sky was full of stars, brilliant and spectacular. The guests sat quietly in it, as if they were in a heavenly palace.

The Groom Forgot the Ring The emcee, Zhou Shang, gave a loud Qin music sound, and the music on the music stage started. The groom entered the seat before the bride. After a short while, the bride entered the hall slowly led by three pairs of bridesmaids. The guests clapped and greeted her. The bride wore a white dress and a veil about two or three feet long. When the emcee sang about exchanging ornaments, the bride took off the ring on her hand and gave it to the groom. The groom also planned to take off the ring in order to exchange it, but he forgot to bring it in a hurry, which caused a temporary laugh.

Mr. Cai's Wonderful Words The marriage witness, Mr. Cai Yuanpei, gave a very mysterious speech, roughly saying that what we people in the world need most now is science and art. Now the groom, Mr. Shen, is studying economics overseas, and the bride, Ms. Li, is studying music at the National Conservatory of Music. Combining science and art in one furnace, the marriage of Shen and Li will definitely form a good family.

A Hall Full of Doctors and Masters The groom, Mr. Shen, once studied at Northwestern University in the United States, so most of the guests who came to watch that day were overseas scholars. There were quite a few doctors and masters. It was a grand and unprecedented occasion. Important figures such as Zhang Fuyun, the director of the Customs Department, and Dr. Zhang Zhongdao, the director of the Nanjing City Education Bureau, also came to watch. The groomsmen were Dr. Ma Zhichao, etc.

Unmarried Couples Accompanying the Hall In the evening, the two families of the man and woman held a banquet at the Xin Xin Restaurant. The seat in the middle was occupied by the groom and bride, and most of those accompanying the new couple were female guests. The unmarried sister-in-law of the bride was also in the seat. When the banquet was half over, the bride's brother was escorted by the guests and also moved to the groom's seat to drink side by side with his fiancée. As a result, a group of relatives and friends toasted the newlyweds on the one hand, and on the other hand, they asked the unmarried couple to raise their glasses and intensify their work. It was also a particularly interesting event.

The Bride's Alcohol Tolerance Is Better Than the Groom's After the new couple finished toasting the guests, Director Zhang Zhongdao and Mr. Ge Gongzhen, recommended by the guests, set the record for toasting the new couple. As a result, a hundred people responded to the call, and male and female relatives and friends came with wine pots and surrounded the new couple. The groom had a very small alcohol tolerance and felt dizzy after drinking only a few glasses. The bride had a very high alcohol tolerance. At first, she drank everything, but later she had to find a way to decline because there were too many people toasting. The banquet ended near midnight.

Impressions of West Lake (4) 158

— Hui Jian

After lunch, I proposed to visit Longjing and buy good tea, so I returned to the boat to Tongji Bridge in Yishanbu. I disembarked and the boatman sought a sedan chair for me, supplemented by a rickshaw. The three of us took turns riding in it and went west along the mountain road. At that time, the scorching sun was shining on our backs and it was very warm. Halfway through, Banxia told me that there were two hungry monks in front of Liu Zhuang's shore, clasping their hands together to ask for money. They were all five or six years old. I remembered Mr. Chen San Yuan's poem: "The setting sun is on the misty shore of the temple, knowing that there are hungry monks who will not return." It was like writing the scene at this time. Everyone sighed. After walking for a few miles, we arrived at Hupao first and then at Dinghui Temple to see its very grand mountain gate. The Jizu Pagoda Courtyard on the right was connected to it like a temple. When we arrived, there was a Westerner and a Chinese sitting in front of the door painting oil paintings with the mountain gate as the background. The green willows shaded the scenery and the interest was great. Entering the temple to Hupao Spring, I saw that the water quality was very light and clear. I tried throwing a copper coin into it, and it turned and fell down like the meaning of Wuxi Spring. After a short visit to the spring, we went out and turned east into a fork in the road. The car could not enter, so Banxia abandoned it. After walking about three or four miles, we arrived at Daren Temple. The abbot of the temple, Tique, was a friend of Banxia. I originally planned to stay overnight at the temple, but he happened to be in the city. A monk guided me and others to visit the so-called Shiwu Cave, which was a cave that could accommodate several square feet of space. It was shaped like a studio. When I entered, I felt a sense of coldness that forced people's hearts to palpitate. Dozens of small Buddhas were engraved on the walls, and the techniques were all worth seeing. After passing Daren Temple, we continued to walk through several villages, where children chased away guests and fat dogs barked at people. Entering the mountains was already very deep. Arriving at Shuile Cave, a monk held a lantern and waited at the entrance of the cave, asking to guide us. The cave was about twenty feet deep, and the height did not touch the head. The monk stopped at a water hole and said that he was afraid of suffocation if he went forward, so he blocked it with rocks. We tried to turn off the lights and indeed felt suffocated and unbearable. Banxia scooped up the water and drank it, saying that it was very sweet. After passing Shuile Cave, we arrived at Yanxia Cave about a mile away. The mountain trees were ferocious here, and all we could see was chaotic clouds. Walking in the mountains was even more difficult. It was already halfway up Nan Gao Peak. I originally planned to visit Lian Temple via the Yangmeiling branch road and visit the Nine Streams and Eighteen Caves. Lao Lan and Banxia both insisted that it was late and they could not do it, so they took another road to Longjing. As soon as we reached the entrance of the village, we saw a tea shop shouting for guests to come in and view it. The best quality tea was called Shifeng Yacha. It was a flag, not a spear. The color was slightly green and the smell was clear and fragrant. The price was one yuan per tael, which was the highest price among Longjing teas. Banxia and I suspected that it was not entirely reliable and abandoned it. When we went out, there was another good tea that could be sold. When we arrived, it was still a tea shop, and the price could not be lowered. Then we were willing to give an extra tael outside of five taels. I and others bought a few taels each as a souvenir of this trip. The shopkeeper quickly led us to visit the well in front of the door, which was Longjing. Most of those who sell tea here have the surname Weng. The mountain is called Wengjiashan, which is three miles away from here and is Xinlongjing. It is said that the tea quality is better than this and the planting is also more effective. Looking at the time, it was already half past five. Banxia and Lao Lan were unwilling to go, so we returned to Tongji Bridge and took the Qianzhou boat back east. It was already dusk. Banxia recited my old poem "The Great Moon Turns Green and Yellow, and All Things Are Like Paintings."

Warmth in the Heart (311) 159

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter Fifteen: Tears Fall All Around for Sad Red Romance, Hearts are Captured by Lingering Green Thoughts

Ling Zhixiang is a grand educator in the world of flowers. In Shanghai's prostitute society, there is a saying that he is a "garbage wagon." The meaning of "garbage wagon" is that he accepts everything, good or bad, beautiful or ugly, without discrimination, just like a garbage wagon on the road that takes in all kinds of dirty and filthy things. That is a madam's way of cursing someone, but the person being cursed does not take offense. Long Ziyun is the opposite of Ling Zhixiang. He does not advocate calling in every madam and singer, like Han Xin commanding troops, the more the better. Instead, he advocates continuing to call on a family once he is acquainted with them. Especially, the ones he calls on are established families in the Shanghai prostitution world. Now he is calling on the Bao family in Puqing Lane. The family has a military background and is known as a warlord family. At this time, there are several families in the northern part of Shanghai that can be called prostitution warlords, such as the Bao family. The so-called Bao family's five clouds have generations of successors, and those who come out seem to each have their own style. All kinds of strange and extravagant costumes are not allowed, nor are they allowed to be too simple and frugal, with an intention to suit both the present and the past. That day, they arrived at a Beijing restaurant on Shilu Road called Yuebinlou. This restaurant was newly built, and the old store was reopening. In Shanghai, whenever a new store opens, everyone wants to make a fuss, as it is human nature to like the new and dislike the old. Moreover, everyone wants to try a new restaurant or bar. New things gradually become old, so the old ones are renovated. The new can also cause a stir for a while, like a restoration era in a country. Chinese merchants used to have a kind of conservatism, believing that the older the signboard, the more valuable it was. Even if the pillars were blackened by smoke and the walls were mottled, they would never repair them, as if repairing them would have a great impact on business. Like the restaurants in the alleys of Shanghai and the small restaurants outside Qianmen in Beijing, they were all like that. Although the cooking was very exquisite, the place was really too difficult. Sometimes it was steamed by various oil fumes, and sometimes the tables and chairs were covered with grease. Moreover, the place was small and not enough to turn around. When there were more customers, their backs touched each other and their clothes brushed against each other. But the more crowded it was, the more prosperous the business became. The shop owners had a kind of superstition, believing that such prosperous business must be due to good feng shui. If they repaired and rebuilt, it would hinder the feng shui. But when it was really dilapidated and there was no room to stand, that feng shui superstition would be broken. Because in the Shanghai concessions, houses had a certain number of years before they had to be demolished and rebuilt. After rebuilding, the house would naturally be brand new, and the rent would also be increased. At that time, the land price would also rise. The shop owners who lived in new houses and paid higher rents might have to add some capital to reorganize their business. So they added a lot of new furniture, opened new sources of income, and even installed a neon sign to illuminate the entrance like daylight. Yuebinlou is also an old store reopening this time. Originally, their food was not bad, so it caused a stir again.

Commercial News

Gold Market in a Week of Finance 160

The changing power is moderate, and the transaction volume is not large. The gold market situation last week was still considered mild, but there was no lack of circling. Only three or four taels were reviewed every day. It coincided with the Western merchants' autumn competition period. From Monday to Wednesday, it was customary for the market to be open for half a day, and colleagues had no large amount of receipts and payments. In fact, the swap period was approaching, and the confrontation between the long and short sides had become a stalemate. Since Tuesday (November 4), the prices of British and American silver have both been reported to be long, and the London shilling has risen sharply by 3.125. The shilling was then quoted half a gear higher. As a result, the gold price had broken through the 80 taels mark, and suddenly it was 74 taels and 9 mace. At that time, large households such as Zhifeng, Yongnei, Xingyuan, Yongyongchengchang, etc. tended to sell off. However, by Thursday, the silver market saw a contraction and the exchange rate contracted by half a gear. Large groups and arbitrageurs in the market scrambled to buy, and the price trended upwards, reaching 85 taels and 8 mace. After that, there was a slight accumulation, but the intentions of the industry were confused and at a loss, as if there was news. The price suddenly showed an unnecessary change. It was found that the total for this week was 10 taels and 0.9 mace. If the result was delayed until Saturday, it was 82 taels and 8 mace, a drop of only 3 mace compared to the previous Saturday. As for the overseas silver market, large bars were long by 1.875 to 1.25, and the price of American silver was long by 2.5. HSBC's listing of shillings had no changes, only long and then short, and the transaction price of the bank was also peaceful. Arbitrageurs in the gold industry sometimes engaged in padding, but the amount was not large. The closing price was initially pressed within 40 taels, then 34-5 taels, and finally 37 taels. The spot red bar trend was not smooth, and the price seemed to be downstream. The term bid only added 12 taels to 11 taels. The general situation of the week is described below:

The swap message is approaching, and the long and short sides are watching. Since Monday, the large bar of silver has not moved, but American silver has been long by 2.5, and the shilling has not moved. The domestic market has also not changed. Guangbang has slightly padded. As for the gold bid, the initial opening for December was 81 taels and 3 mace. Because of the activity of buyers, it was calculated at 82 taels, so the shilling seemed loose and the sellers exceeded the constant, and the price dropped by more than 3 taels, breaking the 80 taels mark. The closing price at noon was 79 taels and a half. In the afternoon, due to the autumn competition holiday, the next day, the buying exceeded the selling and the exchange market loosened. The large bar was long again. At the beginning of the morning, it was tired, but then suddenly it was 74 taels and 9 mace, but it immediately returned to 1-2 taels, and finally it was flat, calculated at 77 taels. It fell for three consecutive days, a total of 7 taels and 2 mace. The gold market on Wednesday had a rebounding trend and once escaped the 80 taels mark, but the large bar continued to be long and the silver price was not good. The market was still flat in the early morning, but later, because the buyers were strong and the bars were particularly lacking, there was a rush of more than 4 taels. The closing price at noon reached 82 taels and 3 mace. From morning to noon, there was a review of 5 taels and 1 mace, an increase of 5 taels and 3 mace compared to the previous day. The next day, the large bar and the silver price both contracted, and the shilling also contracted by half a gear. The gold market has resumed full-day business because the autumn competition has passed. The initial opening rose by 1 tael and 9 mace. Later, Yuanheng, Shunli, Taikang, Run, etc. scrambled to buy, and it was discovered that it had reached 85 taels and 8 mace. However, after noon, it retreated by 2-3 taels, and Zhifeng, Yongyongfeng, etc. sold off. The afternoon was flat, only with an increase of 2 taels. The final calculation was 83 taels and 1 mace, a continued increase of 8 mace. But the market situation was mild, and the difference for the whole day was only 3 taels. On Friday, the large bar returned long and the silver price did not move. The gold market situation was very flat, only with a circling of 2 taels, and the price stood between 83 and 4 taels. There were few transactions, but the closing price was 84 taels, an increase for three consecutive days compared to the previous day. The increase on this day was only 9 mace. On Saturday, the silver market and the exchange ticket department did not change. The gold market seemed to be latent. It had already risen repeatedly and then reversed. The initial price was around 84 taels. By noon, Taiheng, Yuan, Yuanmao, Yongzhifengyong, etc. had suddenly sold off. People's hearts were easily empty, and the market atmosphere was weakened as a result. The result was 82 taels and 8 mace, a drop of 1 tael and 2 mace and a half. Art World

About Sinclair Lewis 206

— Ling Dai

The winner of the 1930 Nobel Prize in Literature was announced on November 5th. It is Sinclair Lewis, an American novelist.

In the days leading up to this announcement, before the news was released, the most promising candidate for this year's Nobel Prize in Literature, according to newspaper reports, was the American Theodore Dreiser and the newly added member of the French Academy, the poetic philosopher Paul Valéry. However, the announced news differs greatly from the oversensitive reports of newspaper reporters. Let me briefly introduce Sinclair Lewis, the recent recipient of the highest honor in world literature.

The Nobel Prize in Literature began in 1900, and this year marks the thirtieth time it has been awarded. In the past thirty times, those who have received this high honor include five Germans, five French, two English, three Norwegians, two Swedes, and one each from Denmark, Italy, Spain, Poland, Ireland, Switzerland, Belgium, and India.

From the nationalities of the past thirty winners, we see that only one belongs to a so-called oppressed ethnic group, a person of color, namely the Indian Tagore. In this tabulation, we do not see the selection of a literary figure of American nationality, which holds hegemony in the world's economy and politics. We might attribute this fact to Europe's longstanding disdain for the United States, or we can place its explanation on the other hand, in the Americans' focus on material or mechanical enjoyment and neglect of literary and artistic cultivation. But these explanations are not to the point.

In fact, in terms of literature and art themselves, their development and prosperity must accompany economic development and prosperity. This is very evident in literary history. For example, the Elizabethan era was the golden age of English literature, and its prosperity was precisely because the operation of new colonies everywhere increased its wealth and led to economic prosperity. The relationships between Boccaccio of Italy, Cervantes of Spain, and others can be determined by the economic circumstances of their time. The most characteristic point is that the economic form of the early era can determine the content and characteristics of the literature of a certain era. For example, Boccaccio's "Decameron" could only exist in the era of commercialism, and would never have occurred in the feudal era of theocracy before the development of commercialism.

Today, the hegemony of the world economy has shifted from England, based on the textile industry, to the United States, based on the steel industry. Therefore, in politics, England's traditional maritime power policy, no matter how vast its colonies or territories, has to advocate equality of Anglo-American power due to changes in economic circumstances. Of course, the development of art and literature is bound to accompany this unfolding economic situation.

Regarding this historical demarcation, we can divide it with the election of Roosevelt as President. Since Roosevelt, the economic and political power of the United States has become increasingly prosperous. At the same time, the United States has also made new contributions in art and literature. However, this kind of political, economic, and cultural strength gradually attracted the world's attention after Versailles, and finally, this high literary prize was awarded to the American novelist Sinclair Lewis, the first American literary figure to receive this Nobel Prize in Literature.

The Swedish Academy's awarding of the Nobel Prize in Literature to an American literary figure who has been looked down upon, at least (or perhaps oversensitively) has the following significance:

(1) As the political and economic hegemony of the United States rises daily, and for considerations of diplomacy or international relations, it is timely to award this prestigious literary prize to an American literary figure. Behind this, the awarding of this literary prize contains a certain political meaning (in fact, the reason why last year's literary prize was given to Thomas Mann, a German literary figure, can also be said to contain a certain political meaning). (2) The form, style, and content of American literature, which has accompanied the development of the American economy, have been generally noticed and recognized, and the status of the United States in world literature must be acknowledged.

Now let me briefly introduce Lewis's life. Sinclair Lewis was born in 1885 in a small town in Minnesota. From an early age, he was immersed in the environment of the petty bourgeoisie of small towns in the American West. Minnesota is in the northwestern United States, located in the upper reaches of the Mississippi River. The climate is cold early, and it is also a very large plain, so his cold writing style may have been cultivated in this environment. Later, he entered Yale University in the East and obtained a Bachelor of Arts degree in 1907. After graduating from university, he worked as a reporter for a newspaper in New Haven, where the university was located, and also worked as a reporter for the "Bulletin" newspaper and the Associated Press in San Francisco. Later, he was the editor of magazines such as "Transatlantic Tales" and "Volta Review". Later, he was an editor at the publishing house George H. Doran Co.

His first novel was published in 1914 ("Our Mr. Wrenn"), but the key to his fame was "Main Street".

After the publication of "Main Street", he published "Babbitt" in 1922. Later, "Elmer Gantry" in 1927 received even more general attention. In the book, he more forcefully criticized the hypocrisy of American clergymen. In addition, other works include "Arrowsmith", "The Man Who Knew Coolidge", "Mantrap", "Dodsworth", etc. He also wrote plays. His Hobohenia was performed in New York in 1919.

In Lewis's novels, we can see that his writing style is euphemistic and powerful, cold and clever. In American literature, he has indeed pioneered a new style, which can shine brightly with Edgar Allan Poe and Walt Whitman, one after the other. His novels are of course very popular.

Art Section Guidelines 207

(1) Articles should be limited to news, commentary, and introductions related to recent domestic and foreign art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature.

(3) Photos should be limited to recent portraits of domestic and foreign writers and their works, as well as various photographs related to writing.

(4) The number of words per article should not exceed 2,000.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the paper.

(6) Manuscripts should not be written horizontally or carelessly. Western text can be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

Social News

In Xuzhou 208

— Moye

Tongshan Correspondence

Xuzhou is an important strategic point for the rear defense of the Central Army, located at the intersection of the Jinpu and Longhai Railways. Its military significance is self-evident. However, when the troops under Yan and Feng were fighting, although they took this as their destination, they were not actually subjected to military panic. However, most of the wounded soldiers transported back from the front line were left here, so the market could not avoid being disturbed. Now that most of the wounded soldiers have returned to their teams, and the Xuzhou Headquarters has also been withdrawn last week, the various military facilities have disappeared. After arriving in Xuzhou, the reporter's first goal was to investigate the number of wounded soldiers and those who returned to their teams after recovery, in order to observe the content and strength of the army. The second was to investigate the wartime layout and deployment. Now, the findings of the investigation are recorded as follows:

1. Brief Statistics on Wounded Soldiers and Returns to Duty: The total number of wounded soldiers in the Central Army exists in the Health Department of the General Headquarters. The exact number is still unavailable. According to a more reliable investigation, it should be over 50,000. The total number of returns to duty is also difficult to know in detail. However, taking Xuzhou as an example, in the past four months, the number of officers and soldiers who recovered from their injuries and returned to their units was only 11,871. The total number of wounded soldiers accommodated in Xuzhou in the seven hospitals before and after was more than 30,000.

The distribution of wounded soldiers returning to duty in Xuzhou in the past four months is approximately as follows: From June 9th to July 27th, a total of 3,046 officers and soldiers. From July 27th to August 31st, a total of 1,925 officers and soldiers. From September 1st to October 1st, a total of 550 officers and soldiers. From October 1st to October 20th, a total of 1,350 officers and soldiers. The above numbers are the survey data of the Xuzhou Wounded Soldier Inspection Office and are very accurate. Furthermore, observing the eighth month after the establishment of the office on June 9th, the investigation of wounded soldiers leaving the hospital is approximately as follows: 6,409 admitted, 5,651 discharged, 2,309 returned to duty, 2,015 transferred, 168 deaths, 1 dismissed, and 164 deserted. Furthermore, observing the number of officers and soldiers returning to duty in each unit based on the army as a standard, from June 9th to July 7th, the number of officers who returned to duty due to injury was: 59 from the 1st Division, 26 from the 2nd Division, 24 from the 3rd Division, 21 from the 11th Division, 26 from the 64th Division, and the remaining units with less than 20 people were not listed. As for soldiers, 705 from the 1st Division, 485 from the 2nd Division, 395 from the 3rd Division, 115 from the 9th Division, 409 from the 11th Division, and 217 from the 64th Division. Those with less than 200 people were generally omitted. In total, there were 200 officers and 2,846 soldiers. The above is for the month of July. Furthermore, in August, the number of officers who returned to duty due to injury was 70 from the 1st Division, 19 from the 2nd Division, and 20 from the 3rd Division, totaling 170. The number of soldiers was 657 from the 1st Division, 133 from the 2nd Division, 158 from the 3rd Division, 157 from the 11th Division, and 173 from the 9th Division, totaling 1,759. The numbers of officers and soldiers from each unit that were less than 20 and 200 respectively were omitted. Note that the above numbers only refer to the Xuzhou area and cannot be generalized to the entire matter. However, Xuzhou is the center of the rear hospitals, and the number of people is also the largest. Officers and soldiers on the Jinpu and Longhai lines are all present, so it is still a material for inference and reference. Readers should know that the units of the Central Army that participated in the war are as follows: three teaching divisions (1st, 2nd, and 3rd divisions), and the National Revolutionary Army's 1st, 2nd, 3rd, 5th, 46th, 7th, 8th, 9th, 10th, 11th, 12th, 13th, 21st, 23rd, 26th, 41st, 42nd, 45th, 47th, 52nd, 54th, 55th, 60th, 63rd, 64th, 65th, and 66th divisions, totaling twenty-one direct armies. In addition, there were also teaching regiments, guard brigades, the 2nd Army Corps, the 1st Route Cavalry Brigade, independent brigades, the 15th Independent Brigade, the Shandong Garrison, the Joint Army Convoy, the 15th Route Headquarters, the 12th Route Headquarters, the 11th Route Headquarters, the 6th Independent Brigade, the Independent Artillery Regiment, the Cavalry Brigade, and the Central Military Academy Headquarters, etc., which were added to the front line one after another. According to the previous table, it can be known that the divisions with the largest number of wounded soldiers and officers are the 1st Division of Liu Zhi, the 2nd Division of Gu Zhutong, the 3rd Division of Chen Jicheng, and the 11th Division of Chen Cheng. Among them, the losses suffered by the units of Liu Zhi, Chen Cheng, and Chen Jicheng were the largest. The larger number of officers and soldiers returning to duty can prove their bravery in combat and strict discipline.

2. Wartime Deployment: Xuzhou is the throat of Nanjing, and the Central Army is bound to defend it to the death. However, because it is far from the front line, the deployment is not urgent. There was a period when the Jin Army bypassed Gunzhou and intended to spy on Tongshan. The Central Government moved the trenches in the Haozhou area, extending them to the north of Tongshan and the shores of Weihu Lake for a total of four to five hundred li. Even within the territory of Tongshan County, the digging and excavation circled for more than a hundred li. Tens of thousands of soldiers were stationed to the west of the station. The reporter once visited and saw that it was about eight feet deep and wide, which was far superior to the five ditches in the Guide area. In addition, the wartime equipment that is commendable is the airfield, which is also located to the west of the station and is the base camp of the Longhai Air Force team. On the first day the reporter came to Xuzhou, he saw red-tailed, blue-winged planes soaring above, transmitting orders to various departments, and they no longer frightened the residents.

Since He Yaozu returned to Beijing and the Xuzhou Headquarters was abolished, Xuzhou seems to have returned to a state of peace. However, in reality, the inns are still occupied by the army, and the cost of living is extremely high. The room rate in ordinary hotels is more than two yuan, which is not comparable to the eight-corner rooms in Pingpu. The prices of all daily necessities and rickshaws are also high. The reason is that on the one hand, the transient officers in the army raised prices, and on the other hand, the sellers, due to the impact of the war, were eager to make up for the losses after the restoration of order. Recently, because the garrison commander Song Runtian followed Chen Tiaoyuan's team to take up a new post in Anhui, the business community was busy preparing a farewell party. At the same time, the 52nd Division of Ye Kaixin, which took over the defense of Xuzhou, has arrived, and its deputy commander Han Deqin came first.

Book Review

Grassland Weekly 209

— Nan Xin

Volume 3, Issues 12 & 13

The content of (Grassland Weekly) has been particularly brilliant and substantial in the most recently published two issues. Originally, it actively strived to promote nationalist literature and poetry. Among the small weekly publications, we must first recommend (Grassland), which already has a long history. The poems published by Tang Zeng on Issue 12, though starting from a slightly lower point, undoubtedly firmly grasp the core of nationalism in their ideology. The observation expressed in the artistic presentation of the poems as a whole is exceptionally compact. This is what is meant by poetic skill. Now, let's dissect the content of these two poems meticulously, thereby glimpsing the powerful guidance possessed by the poet.

The first poem is titled (Come, Revolutionary Brothers). Just seeing this title makes us readers feel a surge of heroic and passionate spirit, as if we are about to gather with brothers who are fighting for the revolution and rush forward. This is, of course, a revolutionary battle arising for the freedom of our entire Chinese nation.

The entire poem is divided into eleven sections. The author uses poetry to promote nationalist literature as the main theme. Using synthesis, many worthy expressions of scattered and unrestrained forms are appended with elements of beauty, forming a compact and coherent poem. Each section mostly encourages (Revolutionary Brothers) to strive greatly for the glory of the Chinese nation. This, of course, should be advanced unyieldingly. Simply put, the entire poem centers on (encouraging revolutionaries). Secondly, relying on the author's intense emotions and rich imagination, it depicts many remnants that should be washed away and hinder the development of the nation's future. Without hesitation, the gray, decadent clothes must be taken off, and the listless sorrow must be eliminated. In particular, one must have a heart of upward striving courage. At the same time, how to break through the barriers of the enemy and how to build our own defense fortifications for the war for the country. This powerful narrative method supplements the shortcomings of the expressed central idea. To summarize this poem, it undoubtedly possesses several necessary conditions for nationalist poetics. Now, let's quote the first two sections to make the reader understand the poem's heroic and impassioned nature.

Come, Revolutionary Brothers

Come, Revolutionary Brothers

Drink a glass of fine grape wine to the fullest

Chew a piece of bright red meat with heroic abandon

This contains the blood of martyrs

This shines with the iron of the nation

Drink, rush to the forefront of fighting for the country's glory

Drink, rush to the forefront of fighting for the country's glory

Come, Revolutionary Brothers

Come, Revolutionary Brothers

Lie drunk on the battlefield, admiring the beautiful moon in the blue sky

Walk barefoot by the sea, anticipating the night scene amidst the sounds of war

This leaps with the light of hope

This reveals intense passion

Look, reflecting the tragic image of national victory

Look, reflecting the tragic image of national victory

In terms of form, this poem has broken the old conventions and created a new style. The second poem is (The Brilliant Light of Iron and Blood Intertwines). This title contains an unparalleled deep meaning. The entire poem completely depicts the leaping of (iron and blood) on the battlefield, the spirit and feats of martyrs, the ferocious faces of imperialists, etc., all powerfully portrayed. The entire poem is even more intense than the previous one, and the style has also been changed. It has indeed opened a new path in Chinese poetry. For example:

Quickly spur your horse and whip it forward

Relying on iron hooves

Trample through the waning moon for thousands of miles

Relying on a steel-forged head

Break through the stone walls of ten thousand mountains

Sing a thread of golden melody

Run forward

Drink the blood of the barbarian with pain

Run forward

Execute the tyrant

It is truly not easy to express such power in very short lines. The following sections are all lively and delightful. Due to the limited space of this publication, they will not be cited one by one. However, in the present time of striving to promote nationalist literature and art, poems describing the various situations on the battlefield like this

are very urgently needed, and we hope to see them often on (Grassland) with those who love poetry.

The thirteenth issue contains Huang Yuruo's creation (Comrades on the Same Road), which depicts the (May Thirtieth) massacre incident, completely centered on nationalism. For such a major historical fact of the Chinese nation's battle with imperialism, we need to re-evaluate it. This can awaken our compatriots and prevent foreigners from mocking us Chinese for only having five minutes of passion. We have read many of Huang's works on (Grassland), and this one is particularly powerful because the author is exceptionally skilled in technique.

Prenuptial Notes 210

— Nan Xin

Published by the Grassland Society

The recent Chinese creative world seems to have gradually flourished and then declined. This is because various new bookstores nowadays mostly pay attention to textbooks for various subjects in universities and middle schools, as well as general children's literature. Therefore, short and long creative works are rarely seen by our readers. However, Jin Kuansheng's (Prenuptial Notes) suddenly appeared before our eyes in such a seemingly quiet Chinese creative world. This is truly a very gratifying thing, especially for those of us who love to read literary works.

Jin's book is a kind of diary-style writing, and the language is extremely natural and fluent. When we read each paragraph separately, they are many essays with lasting meaning. If we read them continuously in one breath, then it becomes a diary-style novella. In fact, describing in this way, whether in writing style or meaning, easily reveals the author's unique strengths. In the subtle parts of this (Prenuptial Notes), it can be seen that the author is truthfully depicting it, with no traces of empty embellishment revealed in the words and lines.

The author wrote down a memorable page of his own love history without any concealment. The reason why the author got engaged was really to cherish Ms. Jiang's life experience and comfort his parents' old age. Now let's first look at what he recorded below:

I am not young anymore. I have not relieved my parents of any of their burdens. The eldest son is twenty-four years old (lunar calendar) and has not yet been engaged. Parents very much hope that their son will marry and become an adult. My youth has passed, and the fire of my passionate youth has almost been extinguished. My time can no longer love young girls. Young girls are materials that increase sorrow and trouble for me. Young girls can mislead my great future. My time should be spent studying hard and cultivating myself in order to prepare to contribute to mankind, seek happiness for society, and add glory to the country... I have had several young girls. Have the experiences with several young girls been from beginning to end? Several young girls have wasted excessive amounts of money in vain... Sweet memories add another layer of bitterness to the bitterness. When I examine myself in the middle of the night, I am both ashamed and regretful. I agreed to my parents' engagement, and I will have a proper place to return.

After reading the above section, we can know that the author himself is repenting of his past loves, and at the same time, he is also hoping that his future will be glorious. Therefore, his engagement with Ms. Jiang is seeking a proper destination. These are all words of true feelings. Below is a description of the life experience of his fiancée:

Her situation is bitter. When she was eleven years old, her loving mother passed away. Until she was nineteen years old, she lived a school life. Fortunately, her father loved her so that she did not suffer too much... She was restricted by her family and treated coldly by her stepmother. She had no sisters or brothers to talk and laugh with, and she had no aunts to confide in. From the year she was nineteen, she worked as a teacher. A young girl who had not experienced the world was lonely and bitter, talking to herself. Who was her comfort? The teacher's life was suitable and devoted to her. She found a glimmer of light in the lonely, melancholy, and desperate situation.

From these two sections, we can also glimpse the author's sympathy for his fiancée's desolate life experience. The author nakedly presents these moving scenes before our eyes.

This book is beautifully printed and can truly be used as a prenuptial memento. There are also many new descriptions in the content.

Manuscript Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Reviews 211

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all books and newspapers on politics, economics, law, science, education, etc., are included in the introduction. However, frivolous books and newspapers will not be introduced.

(2) Pictures are limited to the latest works of new artists at home and abroad and related illustrations related to the text.

(3) Texts on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Pictures and photos are limited to those related to the text.

(5) Each text should not exceed three thousand words.

(6) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(7) Do not write the manuscript horizontally, and do not use cursive characters. Western text can be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(8) Do not use watercolors for pictures, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black drawings.

(9) Please indicate "Book and Newspaper Introduction Compilation Department" when submitting manuscripts.

(10) Whether the manuscript is published or not, it will not be returned. If it needs to be returned, please declare in advance and attach sufficient postage.

(11) Remuneration for texts is divided into three types: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words.

The same applies to each picture and photo. There are also special remuneration manuscripts.
